Now I understand how `getApiError` works. Looking at lines 19-45:\n\n```typescript\nexport const getApiError = (e?: any) => {\n    if (!e) {\n        return {};\n    }\n    const { data, status } = e;\n\n    if (!data) {\n        return {\n            status,\n        };\n    }\n\n    const { Error: errorMessage, Code: errorCode, Details: errorDetails } = data;\n\n    if (!errorMessage) {\n        return {\n            status,\n        };\n    }\n\n    return {\n        status,\n        code: errorCode,\n        message: errorMessage,\n        details: errorDetails,\n    };\n};\n```\n\nSo `getApiError` returns an object with `status` and/or `code` properties. If the error is falsy (undefined, null, etc.), it returns an empty object `{}`. If the error doesn't have a `status` property, it still returns an object but without `status`.\n\nNow looking at the current implementation in observeApiError:\n```typescript\nconst { status, code } = getApiError(error);\n\nif (!status || status === -1 || error?.name === 'AbortError' || ignoreCodes.includes(code)) {\n    return;\n}\n```\n\nThe line `if (!status ...)` will catch:\n- Cases where `status` is undefined (when getApiError returns an object without status)\n- Cases where `status` is 0 (falsy value)\n- Cases where `status` is -1\n\nWait, but in the tests, there's a difference between `observeApiError` and `observeError`:\n\nFor `observeApiError`:\n- Test on line 30-34: \"ignores reporting if status is 0\" - expects 0 calls\n\nFor `observeError`:\n- Test on line 109-114: \"returns failure if if status is 0\" - expects 1 call with 'failure'\n\n\nSo the implementations need to be different. In `observeApiError`, the early return condition `!status` treats 0 as falsy and skips reporting entirely. But `observeError` should report even when status is 0, only returning early if status is completely undefined or null. The key distinction is that `observeApiError` filters out status 0 responses while `observeError` treats them as valid failures. - If status is 0, it's falsy, so metricObserver gets called with 'failure'\n- If status is -1, it's truthy, so we skip that block and call observeApiError instead, which has its own check for -1 that prevents any observer calls\n\nThe test expects no calls when status is -1, and the current code achieves this by routing -1 through observeApiError where it gets filtered out early.\n\nLet me verify this against a few specific test cases to confirm the behavior is correct.\n\nWhen error is undefined in observeApiError, the early return `if (!error)` prevents any metric observation.
